  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_80778117" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/80778117" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/80778117?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">teen girls who like reading about clothes, parties, hot guys and hooking up </span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tatiana by: </span>
      Heather
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2009">2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=romancelandia">romancelandia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer80778117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11065238620868637731">This second "Blue Bloods" book has one major improvement - the number of pages dedicated to describing various pieces of clothing is reduced from about 150 pages in the first book to about 50. The rest of the book is of the same quality - same flat characters, same obsession with parties, expensive things and good looks, same absence of noticeable climax, and, sadly, same plot (or lack of it).<br/><br/>What goes for these books however is a very intriguing new take on vampire lore. It is obvious this lore</span>
  <span id="freeText11065238620868637731" style="display:none">This second "Blue Bloods" book has one major improvement - the number of pages dedicated to describing various pieces of clothing is reduced from about 150 pages in the first book to about 50. The rest of the book is of the same quality - same flat characters, same obsession with parties, expensive things and good looks, same absence of noticeable climax, and, sadly, same plot (or lack of it).<br /><br />What goes for these books however is a very intriguing new take on vampire lore. It is obvious this lore comes to de la Cruz easily. Her mythology is elaborate and inventive, skillfully mixed with theology. Unfortunately it is wasted on the stories which are nothing more than fluff. Because seriously, how many centuries will it take these millenia-old fallen angels to redeem themselves in the eyes of God if all they seem to care about are: clothes, modeling, parties, and hooking up? My guess is: very many centuries (and books).<br /><br />In spite of the obvious low quality of the books, I am still moving on to book 3. Mainly because they are entertaining albeit mindless page turners. However these books will never be something that I re-read, spend my money on or recommend to my friends. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11065238620868637731" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_53420108" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/53420108" />
    <a title="PurplyCookie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2214498-purplycookie"><img alt="PurplyCookie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415491715p2/2214498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/53420108?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PurplyCookie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PurplyCookie" href="/user/show/2214498-purplycookie">PurplyCookie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781423101277" href="/book/show/3967980-masquerade">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=book-series">book-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=angelology">angelology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=vampire">vampire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=boarding-school">boarding-school</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer53420108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11471965368863347577"><b>"Masquerade"</b> is the second installment In De La Cruz's <b>"Blue Bloods" </b>series. It continues where <b>"Blue Bloods" </b>left off, when Schuyler's grandmother was reprocessed through the vampire cycle, where she would eventually be reborn, after an interrupted attack by a Silver Blood. She (along with her Conduit Oliver) goes on a mission in Venice to find her grandfather, Lawrence Van Alen. Her grandmother's last plea was that Schuyler find her grandfather so that he could save the Blue Bloods from the Cr</span>
  <span id="freeText11471965368863347577" style="display:none"><b>"Masquerade"</b> is the second installment In De La Cruz's <b>"Blue Bloods" </b>series. It continues where <b>"Blue Bloods" </b>left off, when Schuyler's grandmother was reprocessed through the vampire cycle, where she would eventually be reborn, after an interrupted attack by a Silver Blood. She (along with her Conduit Oliver) goes on a mission in Venice to find her grandfather, Lawrence Van Alen. Her grandmother's last plea was that Schuyler find her grandfather so that he could save the Blue Bloods from the Croatan, or the Silver Bloods. But what they find is a man who does not want to come back to a group that shunned his ideas and cast him out. <br /><br />Back in Duschene, the intrigues thicken. Bliss' mystery deepens, including the identity of her mother and the whys and wherefores of all of her nightmares and blackouts. Jack's infatuation with Schuyler is given more significance, and I liked the reasoning behind it. The connection between Mimi and Jack through all of their life cycles is explored well, but apart from that their characters are much the same. I was hoping for more development from Mimi. She's turning out to be one of the most one-dimensional characters I've had the chance of reading. Best friend and Conduit Oliver takes a familiar and predictable turn in regards to his feelings for our heroine, Schuyler, who grows a bit more spine. Her character is more well-defined here, and her relationships with Oliver and Jack are explored in more depth in this novel though with no real resolution. <br /><br />The book didn't start off on the right foot for me because it violated a pet peeve of mine. In the first few pages, it almost blatantly dumped everything on the reader that had happened in the previous book. If people aren't smart enough to start with the first book in the series, then let them swim without a lifejacket and try to pick up what's going on. It felt like a waste of time reading the same descriptions repetitively. <br /><br />There are a couple of divergences so Bliss and Schuyler can pursue modeling careers which adds nothing to the plot. It felt like the author knew the fashion world settings and couldn't help but show off her knowledge, even though it had nothing to do with the story. Lastly, the arrival of a new boy at school feels contrived--a means to a certain end--and its starting to feel a tad too deux et machina to me. <br /><br />That said, I think it is time I abandon this series. It was only the vampire lore which has made me buy the sequel but unfortunately De La Cruz's writing style frustrates me to no end. She could've ended the series with the sequel or maybe with the next one, making this a trilogy, but instead she's stretching the plot too thin with news of more books to come. I'm sure there are far more superior vampire fiction out there; I just need to explore my options. <br /><br /><br /><u>Book Details: </u><br /><br /><u>Title</u> Masquerade (Blue Bloods, Book 2)<br /><u>Author</u> Melissa De La Cruz<br /><u>Reviewed By</u> Purplycookie</span>
  <a data-text-id="11471965368863347577" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12216733777525953941">Melissa dela Cruz, this is a filler right?<br/><br/>Come on, nothing really happen in this book. I guess I just have to read the next one since many of my friends considered Book 3 as the best out of the series .<br/><br/>I just don't like that majority of the book was all about partying and hooking up (meh that's pretty much it).<br/><br/>I really also don't have a favorite character atm so to speak.   <span id="freeText12216733777525953941" style="display:none">Melissa dela Cruz, this is a filler right?<br /><br />Come on, nothing really happen in this book. I guess I just have to read the next one since many of my friends considered Book 3 as the best out of the series .<br /><br />I just don't like that majority of the book was all about partying and hooking up (meh that's pretty much it).<br /><br />I really also don't have a favorite character atm so to speak. None of them really strike me as interesting enough to held my interest. And I just felt that the character are very similar to the other characters of YA books I've already read.<br /><br />Schuyler= Zoey, Rose, Ever, Clary<br />Bliss= Lissa<br />Mimi= Aphrodite<br />Jack= Edward, Erik, Jace <br />Oliver= Heath, Simon, Mason<br />Kingsley= Adrian<br />Allegra= Clary's Mom<br /><br />I guessed my disappointment was due to the fact that I've read too many YA books lately and it just so happen that when I've read this one it will always be subjected to comparison and yeah it just that I didn't felt surprised or thrilled. It just so happen that I read it recently so it was just very unfortunate, I can assume that if I read it before Twilight, Vampire Academy or House of Night it can be one of the vampire series I would rate higher.<br /><br />But still I find the book very sexy and still it was a bit different because it talks more about fashion and the vampires are associated with fallen angels and I really loved the author's writing style it was not annoying and I really like how she describe dresses and gowns that sort of stuff.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12216733777525953941" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_84479394" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/84479394" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2638828-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590292807p2/2638828.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/84479394?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/2638828-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781423101277" href="/book/show/3967980-masquerade">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer84479394" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11530958766213357634">While the vampire lore was pretty much all that kept me going while reading <i>Blue Bloods</i>, I found a little more to appreciate while reading its sequel, <i>Masquerade</i>. Granted, this book isn't perfect, but it is a slight step up.<br/><br/>One big thing I noticed was the minimal designer name-dropping. It worked against the previous novel, basically since it made the characters even more distant and unrelatable (except the fact that they're, you know, vampires and all), since I don't think any reader had any id</span>
  <span id="freeText11530958766213357634" style="display:none">While the vampire lore was pretty much all that kept me going while reading <i>Blue Bloods</i>, I found a little more to appreciate while reading its sequel, <i>Masquerade</i>. Granted, this book isn't perfect, but it is a slight step up.<br /><br />One big thing I noticed was the minimal designer name-dropping. It worked against the previous novel, basically since it made the characters even more distant and unrelatable (except the fact that they're, you know, vampires and all), since I don't think any reader had any idea who those designers were anyway. Also, it sped the story along, since the plot wasn't stalled to go into laborious descriptions of every article of clothing and accessory everyone was wearing. Keep in mind that outfit descriptions are in plenty, however, just not to the extent of this novel's predecessor.<br /><br />With any series, it's nice to revisit characters and their many subplots, and it was nice to do that with <i>Masquerade</i>. I found myself caring a little more about characters, even petty things like (-gasp-) if Schuyler and Oliver were going to get together. All the subplots that were hinted at in <i>Blue Bloods</i> are fleshed out in this novel as well, and I like how they are developing so far.<br /><br />Of course, the saving grace of this whole series is the vampires Melissa de la Cruz has created. They’re probably some of the most inventive and interesting supernatural creatures in YA literature. The best parts of these books are learning about their pasts, how they fell from Heaven, their memories of past reincarnations, etc.<br /><br />However, the lack of any climax or satisfying conclusion whatsoever left something to be desired. The main plot of this series seems to only be who the murderous Silver Blood is, and that doesn't seem to have enough substance to sustain a series like this. <i>Masquerade</i> kind of runs the reader in a circle and leaves them right where they started - knowing nothing (except, at the end, you do have one suspect). I don't know, maybe the plot will flesh out into something more, but for the time being, it doesn't seem to have enough substance.<br /><br />Also, what was the point of the Masquerade ball? Its only point seemed to be the filling of the first 150 pages. Well, I suppose it also shows how much these fallen angels love to party down, but I think anyone could have figured that out by now, since that’s all they seem to do, except maybe buy designer clothes. Do these people seriously except to get back into Heaven?</span>
  <a data-text-id="11530958766213357634" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2622152401309741815">Reviewed by Randstostipher "tallnlankyrn" Nguyen for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>When we last left off with Schuyler Van Alen, she was just getting used to the news of being a Blue Blood, or what we normally label them as, a vampire. She gets invited into the New York Blood Bank Committee and, before she knows it, Schuyler is swept away into the unknown world of the Blue Bloods. Unfortunately, it seems like Schuyler discovered her true self at the wrong time, since three Blue Blood teens have been murdered.</span>
  <span id="freeText2622152401309741815" style="display:none">Reviewed by Randstostipher "tallnlankyrn" Nguyen for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />When we last left off with Schuyler Van Alen, she was just getting used to the news of being a Blue Blood, or what we normally label them as, a vampire. She gets invited into the New York Blood Bank Committee and, before she knows it, Schuyler is swept away into the unknown world of the Blue Bloods. Unfortunately, it seems like Schuyler discovered her true self at the wrong time, since three Blue Blood teens have been murdered. <br /><br />Still not satisfied, Schuyler wants more information for why young vampires are dying and the only way she can find out more is by visiting her grandfather, who lives in Italy. And so in MASQUERADE, Schuyler is off with her best friend to get to the truth. But while Schuyler is trying to learn more about her new world, the Four Hundred Ball is being held in New York, and it seems like the party, before and after, are more than what she bargained for. <br /><br />Of course, with all of this mystery and drama, Schuyler's life also has to be filled with a little boy drama. It's not enough having mixed-up, obnoxious feelings toward Jack, but with the new guy in town, things just happen to get messy. <br /><br />Melissa de la Cruz continues her amazing series, BLUE BLOODS, with full force in MASQUERADE. Some problems are solved while even more are unleashed, and you just can't help but fall deep into this wonderful series. The relationships that Schuyler has with everyone around her are just amazingly sweet. The good part about this series is that there is definitely more to come. The drawback just happens to be waiting for the next one.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2037530809?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MaryJane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MaryJane" href="/user/show/66517426-maryjane">MaryJane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66517426-maryjane?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66517426-maryjane?shelf=pre-goodreads">pre-goodreads</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2037530809" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6856206561391658132">Masquerade was a lot of fun to read. The writing hasn’t improved much from book one, but the characters and the plot sure did! This book had great pacing, and an even amount of plot development as well as scenes showing past events/explanations for things. Nothing ~super~ significant happens in this one, but there is a lot of learning that suggests there are some pretty exciting things coming up next. There also isn’t an enormous amount of character growth in this book, but I feel like the stage</span>
  <span id="freeText6856206561391658132" style="display:none">Masquerade was a lot of fun to read. The writing hasn’t improved much from book one, but the characters and the plot sure did! This book had great pacing, and an even amount of plot development as well as scenes showing past events/explanations for things. Nothing ~super~ significant happens in this one, but there is a lot of learning that suggests there are some pretty exciting things coming up next. There also isn’t an enormous amount of character growth in this book, but I feel like the stage is setting for some major improvements among characters and their relationships with one another. <br />Overall this book is your pretty typical sequel, lots of filler and interaction among the characters. It sets things up nicely for the rest of the series. I left this loving these characters even more than I did at the end of book one. I remembered less of the plot for this book, but it also reminded me of why I loved this series so much, so yeah *shrugs* <br /><br />This review may suggest I wasn’t super crazy about this book, but I devoured it and I really did love it!! There were a lot of surprises in this book that I didn’t remember. Lots of character interactions that had me grinning from ear to ear, I honestly couldn’t get enough of it. I think it was an improvement from book one, just not as wild of a ride. I think I'll skip going crazy about the characters in this one because I know that the next book reveals a LOT of "secrets" and that there are some significant relationship developments (including one of my fave ships ever ayyyyy) </span>
  <a data-text-id="6856206561391658132" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10749987353355691442" style="display:none">I bought this book yesterday and finished yesterday too.<br /><br />Urgh. I was too intrigued by the first book's whole IDEA to let this one go by without a read. I buy books out of habit, one I should VERY much stop until I have read it before since this one too was a waste of my money.<br /><br />Urgh again! More blandness. I want to punch Charles force in the face, slap Mimi and the whole Kingsley thing was random and just .... what was the fracking point? Also, Mimi said in the first book that she couldn't remember anything before Roanoke and now suddenly she remembers ROME and PARADISE and Lucifer himself? WTF again! Mimi just rubs me wrong.<br /><br />de la Cruz focuses to much on random modeling crap and should focus more on scenery and setting and STOP skipping key pieces of time. Like, whole hours will go by and she will sum it up in A sentence. Come on now. Flesh out your stories.<br /><br />I would rather have a story with too much detail than barely any at all.<br /><br />I have read the reviews of the third and have decided that I will go to the library for that one. The other two are going to a friend ... or the trash.</span>

  <span id="freeText3125874187935709519" style="display:none">Blue Bloods are the highest level of elite modern New York society. The teen Blue Bloods attend Duchesne School, enjoy the most fabulous parties and share a dark secret. Blue Bloods are vampires; they literally bleed blue blood and sprout fangs when hungry. But that doesn't stop them from partying in this second installment of Melissa de la Cruz's fantasy/horror series, which has even more mysterious secrets and action than its predecessor. <br /><br />Schuyler Van Alen and her destined human assistant, Oliver, begin the book by traveling to Italy in search of Schuyler's outcast grandfather. Her grandmother just passed away in this cycle and advised her to get help from her grandfather. She finds him, but he doesn't seem to be interested in helping her fight the Silver Bloods, who have tried to get rid of the Blue Bloods throughout history. No one believes her insistence that they're back, but she knows that some teens and her grandmother had help dying from the Silvers. <br /><br />Mimi and Jack Force are leading the Blue Bloods in getting ready for the traditional Four Hundred Ball. They will be presented officially at the ball, with their vampire names and identities. Mimi begins to plan an exclusive afterparty for the teen vampires, but she is most looking forward to letting everyone know that she and Jack are destined to be together from history. He may be attracted to Schuyler, the half-Blue Blood, but in each life he and Mimi have ended up together. <br /><br />Bliss, the Blue Blood who moved from Houston with her Senator father, finds herself in strange locations. One time she wakes up at the bottom of a lake, and an unknown vampire helps her. She blacks out more and more frequently and doesn't know why. She still feels that Dylan, her boyfriend who disappeared in the first book, is alive. He must be the one helping her, she thinks. On a modeling gig with Schuyler, she feeds for the first time with a crew member, only to regret it as they then share a bond. <br /><br />At the afterparty, Schuyler is kissed by a masked vampire, but she thinks it's Jack. He has ignored her ever since she announced her feelings that the Silver Bloods have returned. She grows weaker and weaker as vampire and human mixed bloods fight in her for dominance. It becomes clear that she must feed for the first time on a human. She wants it to be Oliver but wonders if that will change their friendship forever. <br /><br />A very attractive new student, Kingsley, enters Duchesne and gets to know all the important players right away. He encourages Mimi in her jealousy of Schuyler, and when some dark magic affects several of the teens, Mimi lands in serious trouble. Could she really be a Silver Blood? <br /><br />Loyalties are tested, and Schuyler struggles the most with this question. Get ready for more surprises and dark secrets in this compelling series. Fans of both vampire stories and Gossip Girl-type New York chick lit will love these books. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3125874187935709519" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/11717809" />
    <a title="Chelsea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/122606-chelsea"><img alt="Chelsea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454261971p2/122606.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/11717809?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea" href="/user/show/122606-chelsea">Chelsea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/122606-chelsea?shelf=youngadult">youngadult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/122606-chelsea?shelf=contemporaryfiction">contemporaryfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/122606-chelsea?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/122606-chelsea?shelf=2008">2008</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer11717809" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10674443765440815480">This wasn't as good as the first one. I actually went back, and flipped through the first one to make sure I wasn't imagining things. de la Cruz's writing style gets much more stilted and awkward in this book, and her exposition gets much more awkward. The first ten pages are full of INFORMATION BEING THROWN AT YOUR HEAD, HEY GUYS REMEMBER FROM THE LAST BOOK?!?<br/><br/>Maybe I was on less cold medicine this time around, but I wasn't as enthralled. The story is still interesting (I like how de la Cruz wor</span>
  <span id="freeText10674443765440815480" style="display:none">This wasn't as good as the first one. I actually went back, and flipped through the first one to make sure I wasn't imagining things. de la Cruz's writing style gets much more stilted and awkward in this book, and her exposition gets much more awkward. The first ten pages are full of INFORMATION BEING THROWN AT YOUR HEAD, HEY GUYS REMEMBER FROM THE LAST BOOK?!?<br /><br />Maybe I was on less cold medicine this time around, but I wasn't as enthralled. The story is still interesting (I like how de la Cruz worked Roanoke and Croatan into her plot, and I really like the idea that the elite of New York aren't just freakishly rich, they're also kind of, well, freaks.)<br /><br />I didn't like the new developments between Schuyler and Oliver. I really didn't like Schuyler because of it - I'm a sucker for the pining childhood friend, so I came down on Oliver's side.<br /><br />I'm not wildly interested in the namedropping and the clothes, but it certainly serves its place in forming a picture of the world they live in. I could do without the constant reminders that they're all freaking gorgeous. Yeah, yeah. And they have super powers and will live forever, oh, and they're rich. I wish someone in the book would have a flaw besides bad taste in make-out partners.<br /><br />Speaking of their make-out partners - is everyone in this society related? Well, yes. A small population with "bonds" that span centuries isn't anything wildly original. But these pairs are frequently born as twins, which gives it a new twist (for me, at least, since I don't spend much time in the fantasy genre). I'm really interested to see where she goes with it. And by this point, everyone is already related, so there can't be many more DUN DUN DUN moments. ... I think.<br /><br />I certainly plan on reading the rest of the series, because they're fun, light, gossipy books (Gossip Girls with Fangs?), but they make me crave a fat, boring, un-"special" heroine. It'd be a nice change of pace. They're out there somewhere, right? Anyone know any?<br /><br />... I think I took longer writing this review than I did reading the book. Yikes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10674443765440815480" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18775555-trinity?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18775555-trinity?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer777565749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10920335833561355220">I really enjoyed this book much more than I enjoyed the first book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/872333.Blue_Bloods__Blue_Bloods___1_' title='Blue Bloods (Blue Bloods, #1) by Melissa de la Cruz' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blue Bloods</a>. There were some things that I thought were annoying but the rest of the book was really great. It ended with a cliff hanger, which I hate, and the thing with the Silver Bloods is starting to annoy me. <br/><br/><i>Schuyler:</i><br/>Schuyler, in my opinion, was a better character in this book than in Blue Bloods. I really want to know how it goes with her and Jack, but now with Oliver, she just got into one big mess. But I am curious how </span>
  <span id="freeText10920335833561355220" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this book much more than I enjoyed the first book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/872333.Blue_Bloods__Blue_Bloods___1_" title="Blue Bloods (Blue Bloods, #1) by Melissa de la Cruz" rel="nofollow noopener">Blue Bloods</a>. There were some things that I thought were annoying but the rest of the book was really great. It ended with a cliff hanger, which I hate, and the thing with the Silver Bloods is starting to annoy me. <br /><br /><i>Schuyler:</i><br />Schuyler, in my opinion, was a better character in this book than in Blue Bloods. I really want to know how it goes with her and Jack, but now with Oliver, she just got into one big mess. But I am curious how it is going to be with Jack. It was obvious to me who was her sister.<br /><br /><i>Jack:</i><br />I really, really like Jack. I hate the bonding with him and Mimi though. I hop things work out between him and Schuyler. Although, it was pretty weird when the author writes that Jack says he is going to have to pretend that Schuyler doesn't exist, but through the rest of the book he doesn't do that at all. <br /><br /><i>Bliss:</i><br />There are so many clues in front of her and she is being very stupid with not putting in the pieces already. I am still confused with Dylan and her, but I hope to know more about that in the next book. <br /><br /><i>Mimi:</i><br />I do not like Mimi. Why is it that she can start flirting with all the guys she wants to, but doesn't allow Jack to like anybody. She takes things really far, which is good because she is the one in the book that would go to extremes. I am glad I didn't get bored in this book like I did with Blue Bloods. <br /><br />In some of the parts in my review, it may sound that I didn't like the book, I am just critical. I really liked this book a lot. There are lots of cliff hangers by each chapter but then the answer comes within another two chapters. But that ending! I seriously need the next book. I am glad I chose to continue this series. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11010872847832594228">even more drama! schulyer and oliver's relationship takes a twist, lost relatives return, and the monster in bliss' dreams is still around. mimi gets what's coming to her, in a sense, and then, strangely, charles force wants schulyer. <br/><br/>this installment was more action-filled and assumed from the beginning that we knew the characters and the setting. there was no baby-sitter's club-type intro, which i appreciated.   <span id="freeText11010872847832594228" style="display:none">even more drama! schulyer and oliver's relationship takes a twist, lost relatives return, and the monster in bliss' dreams is still around. mimi gets what's coming to her, in a sense, and then, strangely, charles force wants schulyer. <br /><br />this installment was more action-filled and assumed from the beginning that we knew the characters and the setting. there was no baby-sitter's club-type intro, which i appreciated. (i always ended up skipping that part of the book - i knew claudia dressed funky, okay?!) <br /><br />jack is still around and we don't really know why. the blue bloods have their equivalent of a coming-out-deb ball, and the true persona's of mimi, jack, allegra, and the rest are revealed. it's SO COOL to see how she ties this all to a bigger mythology, and how schulyer isn't the same - how she doesn't fit the story. <br /><br />lawrence is awesome, and i so feel for oliver. the silver bloods are a reality, just like cordelia said, and then - just as you are waiting for the big stuff to happen - you are kind of left hanging. it's quick and fun and actually really thoughtful, if you aren't reading it just for the plot. i must admit i do love knowing the setting so well, but it's more than the fact it's set in new york. there are layers to these characters that i feel like we are just beginning to learn, and that's something i felt was missing from both the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22188.Gossip_Girl__Gossip_Girl___1_" title="Gossip Girl (Gossip Girl, #1) by Cecily von Ziegesar" rel="nofollow noopener"> Gossip Girl</a> series. which isn't to say that i didn't read all of those, but this seems to be on a slightly higher intellectual level. <br /><br />or maybe i'm just a sucker for stories about fallen angels. <br /><br />this was a little more over-dramatic and cliched, but it didn't stop me from grabbing book three from the library immediately. </span>

<div id="review_133924212" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/133924212" />
    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3810846-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456131471p2/3810846.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/133924212?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/3810846-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Blue Bloods and Other Vamp Novels Fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Julie by: </span>
      Che Artuz and Szamicaela
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3810846-julie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3810846-julie?shelf=vampire-story">vampire-story</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer133924212&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer133924212" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3468845154276618597">Goodness! I am falling for this book! My oh my! I am now on my third book ^^ yippee and reading it feels no longer a burden. Ha ha! And here comes my review.<br/><br/>The story continues after granny Cordelia’s death and Schuyler with her human conduit/best friend/ secret lover, Oliver went off to Venice, Italy in search for his gramps, famously known as Lawrence Winslow Van Alen. At first the trip was disappointing, gramps does not feel like being cooperative so the two went home pokerfaced and frustrate</span>
  <span id="freeText3468845154276618597" style="display:none">Goodness! I am falling for this book! My oh my! I am now on my third book ^^ yippee and reading it feels no longer a burden. Ha ha! And here comes my review.<br /><br />The story continues after granny Cordelia’s death and Schuyler with her human conduit/best friend/ secret lover, Oliver went off to Venice, Italy in search for his gramps, famously known as Lawrence Winslow Van Alen. At first the trip was disappointing, gramps does not feel like being cooperative so the two went home pokerfaced and frustrated then finally after having a thought or two gramps finally decided to help and that’s it! He’s back to New York, get to live (temporarily) with Schuyler, convincing the conclave of the rampant killings of the Silver Bloods which eventually result to displacing Charles Force of the throne as the Regis (Committee Head) and gramps taking over the position. Meanwhile, the Blue Bloods are busy preparing for the so called Four Hundred Ball also known as Patrician Ball held annually to be attended strictly by their kinds, and during this preparation, Mimi Force is planning on a very secretive yet fun <b>Masquerade</b> to be attended exclusively by the <i>young Blue Bloods</i>. Afterwards, surprising revelations start happening, for one would be Kingsley Drexel Martin’s attendance to Duchesne School, another would be Dylan Ward’s occasional emergences especially inside Bliss’s room. <br /><br />Then after fun came trouble 0_o trouble for the BIATCH Mimi Force! My golly I feel like exulting! Mimi the biatch was up into trouble because of Schuyler, wanting her out of the way for her and Jack Force to live happily ever after. While Schuyler’s in trouble of the slut’s wrath, Jack Force the Casanova is totally helpless because of his fickleness. Why can’t he decide?!! I know Melissa de la Cruz wants us to die of anticipation but I hate him for this. This action of his like “now I love you later I hate you!” he ran hot and cold.<br /><br />Oh well, back to the story. Lucky bitch, after all no harm done to her. Safe and sound and so ungrateful of Sky! Finally, while walking home, after the trial was over Charles Force decided to break the news to her… She’s finally residing with the filthy rich and pompous FORCES!!!…the end. <br /><br /><b>Praises:</b><br /><br />*Schuyler Van Alen’s character has improved A LOT. I love the depth the author has put in her. I feel a pang of guilt after realizing how I bashed her character in the 1st book and now, I think I love her character.<br /><br />*The revelations to Kingsley Drexel Martin’s real motive behind all his mysterious and mischievous actions. And the changing of Lab partners reminds me of hush,hush. Idk w/c book came 1st so I am just saying this because I got to read hush,hush 1st before this one. And after all the trouble of Mimi Force and the trial, Kingsley’s nowhere to find! He was first known as an investigator and now one of the ferocious Silver Bloods! Therefore the story was gripping.<br /><br />*Allegra has 2 Daughters and it turned out to be Bliss! And now Dylan’s alive while Kingsley’s gone missing! Hey what’s happening! I am totally insane of the book now and I am excited to finish the third! <br /><br />*Love MIMI’s MISERY! The best part EVER &gt;:))<br /><br />*Stupid me’s falling for JACK FORCE! &gt;.&lt; <br />My favorite part of the book:<br />The flower giving! Also the part during the blood trial when Sky finally knew all the things Jack Force had done for her. <s>I love Dylan Ward more than him”</s><br /><br />Gawd! I am not furious, I do not hate the book, it’s just that I hate Jack Force ‘coz he’s sexy yet sooooo undecided. Phew! I don’t know who to settle, before I am with Dylan, then came Kingsley and now because of the white roses and the kiss (w/ sky) at the ball!   <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1333094942?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Autumn Byrd" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Autumn Byrd" href="/user/show/34645665-autumn-byrd">Autumn Byrd</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34645665-autumn-byrd?shelf=my-library">my-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1333094942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1155759388127931873"><i>The following review is based off my own opinions, thoughts and reactions. So in other words brace yourself. *There may be inappropriate words such as curse words.* You have been advised in advance.*</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475207809ra/20695315.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Where has this book series been all my life?! Have I been living under a rock or something?! Seriously!<br/><br/>I love, love, <b>LOVE</b> the concept of angels becoming vampires and the fact that there are sibling romances! I love the concept and the whole idea of it. It makes things ten times more interesting, enga</span>
  <span id="freeText1155759388127931873" style="display:none"><i>The following review is based off my own opinions, thoughts and reactions. So in other words brace yourself. *There may be inappropriate words such as curse words.* You have been advised in advance.*</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475207809ra/20695315.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Where has this book series been all my life?! Have I been living under a rock or something?! Seriously!<br><br>I love, love, <b>LOVE</b> the concept of angels becoming vampires and the fact that there are sibling romances! I love the concept and the whole idea of it. It makes things ten times more interesting, engaging and sexual desires become a bright flame.<br><br>I also love the fact that this story-line for this book holds various different emotions as it flows from the various character view points. You really get a sense of how each character is feelings and get a good grasp of their thought process.<br><br>However, the fact that the main heroine is a vampire-human hybrid just blew me out of the water. Nine times out of ten, you hear about the whole werewolf-vampire hybrid combination (in my own opinion that's a bit overrated) so the fact that this author switched things up with a vampire-human hybrid makes this whole series incredibly interesting.<br><br>My only major beef with this book was there could have been more suspense, more love/sexual desire, more action and aggressive approach to give the gnawing feeling to the reader to rush to the end to find out what will happen next.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401916848ra/9868188.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Other than that I think this could be a new favorite series for me. It takes me back to <i>The HOuse of Nights</i> series. So I'm curious to see what will happen in the next book of this series.</span>

<div id="review_241024009" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241024009" />
    <a title="Clarisse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7000702-clarisse"><img alt="Clarisse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573145943p2/7000702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/241024009?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clarisse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clarisse" href="/user/show/7000702-clarisse">Clarisse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer241024009" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16410401360285570325">Masquerade picks up right where Blue Bloods left off, with prepartions for the Four Hundred Ball in full swing while Schuyler Van Alen and her best friend/Conduit Oliver Hazard Perry travel to Italy in search of her Grandfather. The book is told through the alternate points of view of three Blue Blood females: Schuyler, who just found out that she’s a vampire and has started her transition, Mimi Force, the most powerful/popular Blue Blood at their school, and Bliss Llewlyn, Texan daughter of a s</span>
  <span id="freeText16410401360285570325" style="display:none">Masquerade picks up right where Blue Bloods left off, with prepartions for the Four Hundred Ball in full swing while Schuyler Van Alen and her best friend/Conduit Oliver Hazard Perry travel to Italy in search of her Grandfather. The book is told through the alternate points of view of three Blue Blood females: Schuyler, who just found out that she’s a vampire and has started her transition, Mimi Force, the most powerful/popular Blue Blood at their school, and Bliss Llewlyn, Texan daughter of a senator who is newlly transplanted to New York and has found herself under Mimi’s finger. Just like in Blue Bloods, I found the POV switches to be a little distracting, especially because the author always ended each one with a cliffhanger.<br /><br />The relationship between Schuyler and her best friend Oliver grows in the obvious way while developing into a pseudo-love triangle between Schuyler, Oliver, and Jack Force. While Schuyler learns exactly what it means to be a Vampire and what powers she has, she also has to learn to navigate the expected social scene that the Blue Blood committees entail. She’s still on the trail of who is killing Blue Bloods, and they do get closer to the truth in book two.<br /><br />Mimi Force is still a mean girl, but in this book, she’s busy not only planning the Four Hundred Ball and the coming out of her and her twin brother Jack’s true angel identities, but also a Masquerade after party that is invitation only that is sure to cause a stir. She isn’t happy that her brother’s attention has been turned to Schuyler when it should be only on her since they are bond mates, so she sets out to make the new Blue Blood’s life a living hell. She teams up with the new bad boy at school Kingsley to get rid of Schuyler as competition for good.<br /><br />Bliss Llewlyn has blackouts where she can’t remember where she is or what she’s been doing, and her parents tell her it’s all part of the process of becoming a mature vampire. But the nightmares are getting worse and she keeps dreaming of her presumed dead boyfriend Dylan, and she’s not sure what is reality and what’s a dream anymore.<br /><br />The rampant and overused designer label/over the top materialism is toned down in this book, so much so that I barely noticed it in this installment. Schuyler and Oliver are the only characters with real growth throughout this one, but more of the Blue Blood mythology and history is revealed to make it original and interesting. Overall, this was a much better book than the first one, and a solide second book in the series. But it does seem like the material is spread a bit thin and more of these books could have been combined to give a more substantial story. I give this one a four out of five</span>
  <a data-text-id="16410401360285570325" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer933403445" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5239473088576223170"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400448500ra/9677536.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>While I liked this book a lot, for most of the time I've felt like I was reading a filler book. If you guys dont know what a filler means let me explain it to you; they are basically random (anime) events/episodes/arcs/characters that do not happen whatsoever in the manga. They come out when the anime adaptation catches up with the manga and has to make time so the manga artist can get a head with the story.The other reason for fillers are to simply milk an anime for more money. These e</span>
  <span id="freeText5239473088576223170" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400448500ra/9677536.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>While I liked this book a lot, for most of the time I've felt like I was reading a filler book. If you guys dont know what a filler means let me explain it to you; they are basically random (anime) events/episodes/arcs/characters that do not happen whatsoever in the manga. They come out when the anime adaptation catches up with the manga and has to make time so the manga artist can get a head with the story.The other reason for fillers are to simply milk an anime for more money. These episodes are not a part of the original story line, and serve NO PURPOSE in furthering the main story line. <br><br>Was this book truly felt like a filler episode? No, not truly but there were moments,lots of moments made me think I was watching/reading one.<br><br>Nothing worthwhile happens in the book until the end. It often takes you on a completely new (and unnecessary) tangent, taking your mind away from the exciting and important parts in the main storyline. I really like the characters, though. <br><br>What I need from the third book; <br>-Less Oliver, more Jack <br>-Mimi actually growing up and getting over Jack <br>-Less modelling and Gossip Girl style scenes, more sub-plots, more action, more background stories<br>-More Jack/Schuyler scenes <br>-Finding about what the hell is wrong (or special) about Bliss :)<br>-More action!!!<br><br><br></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PlFVlolxAo1pJVgECpYJYQlSWs6LWcOt7nxzkGrKfsgEdzxEMi/L5c4O7GX9YwO+3w29BkXUTcq1AjUhp4mMUg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KSxjXH3mcTCO2EiM5B0JsNugZukJjSpZdbR4c1TRrgATCgqOxri4WCnz/O0T6ANvDf+BIccApD4uyj7CmZJcmg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7509224386635171499">Melissa de la Cruz is the New York Times and USA Today best-selling author of many critically acclaimed and award-winning novels for teens including The Au Pairs series, the Blue Bloods series, the Ashleys series, the Angels on Sunset Boulevard series and the semi-autobiographical novel Fresh off the Boat.<br/><br/>Her books for adults include the novel Cat’s Meow, the anthology Girls Who Like Boys Who Like</span>
  <span id="freeText7509224386635171499" style="display:none">Melissa de la Cruz is the New York Times and USA Today best-selling author of many critically acclaimed and award-winning novels for teens including The Au Pairs series, the Blue Bloods series, the Ashleys series, the Angels on Sunset Boulevard series and the semi-autobiographical novel Fresh off the Boat.<br /><br />Her books for adults include the novel Cat’s Meow, the anthology Girls Who Like Boys Who Like Boys and the tongue-in-chic handbooks How to Become Famous in Two Weeks or Less and The Fashionista Files: Adventures in Four-inch heels and Faux-Pas.<br /><br />She has worked as a fashion and beauty editor and has written for many publications including The New York Times, Marie Claire, Harper’s Bazaar, Glamour, Cosmopolitan, Allure, The San Francisco Chronicle, McSweeney’s, Teen Vogue, CosmoGirl! and Seventeen. She has also appeared as an expert on fashion, trends and fame for CNN, E! and FoxNews.<br /><br />Melissa grew up in Manila and moved to San Francisco with her family, where she graduated high school salutatorian from The Convent of the Sacred Heart. She majored in art history and English at Columbia University (and minored in nightclubs and shopping!).<br /><br />She now divides her time between New York and Los Angeles, where she lives in the Hollywood Hills with her husband and daughter. </span>

Indee<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText17975991521198937429\" style=\"display:none\">When the Mayflower set sail in 1620, it carried on board the men and women who would shape America: Miles Standish; John Alden; Constance Hopkins. But some among the Pilgrims were not pure of heart; they were not escaping religious persecution. Indeed, they were not even human. They were vampires.\nThe vampires assimilated quickly into the New World. Rising to levels of enormous power, wealth, and influence, they were the celebrated blue bloods of American society. \n\nThe Blue Bloods vowed that their immortal status would remain a closely guarded secret. And they kept that secret for centuries. But now, in New York City, the secret is seeping out. Schuyler Van Alen is a sophomore at a prestigious private school. She prefers baggy, vintage clothes instead of the Prada and pearls worn by her classmates, and she lives with her reclusive grandmother in a dilapated mansion. Schuyler is a loner...and happy that way. Suddenly, when she turns fifteen, there is a visible mosaic of blue veins on her arm. She starts to crave raw food and she is having flashbacks to ancient times. Then a popular girl from her school is found dead... drained of all her blood. Schuyler doesn\'t know what to think, but she wants to find out the secrets the Blue Bloods are keeping.
